</div>
<p><b>Ulaanbaatar</b>, formerly romanized as <b>Ulan Bator</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/ secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/uː/ long 'oo' in 'food'">uː</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ər/ 'er' in 'finger'">ər</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a>: <span lang="mn">Улаанбаатар</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Mongolian" title="Help:IPA for Mongolian">[ʊɮɑːm.bɑːtʰɑ̆r]</a></span>, <i>Ulaγanbaγatur</i>, literally "Red Hero") is <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" title="Capital (political)">capital</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Mongolia" title="List of cities in Mongolia">largest city</a>. A municipality, the city is not part of any <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aimags_of_Mongolia" title="Aimags of Mongolia">aimag (province)</a>, and its population as of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> was over 1.3 million, almost half of the country's total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statis.ub.gov.mn_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Statis.ub.gov.mn-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Located in north central Mongolia, the municipality lies at an elevation of about 1,310 metres (4,300 ft) in a valley on the <a href="/wiki/Tuul_River" title="Tuul River">Tuul River</a>. It is the country's cultural, industrial and financial heart, the centre of Mongolia's road network and connected by rail to both the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a> in Russia and the <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_China" title="Rail transport in China">Chinese</a> railway system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Official-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city was founded in 1639 as a nomadic <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Mongolia" title="Buddhism in Mongolia">Buddhist</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhist_monasticism" title="Buddhist monasticism">monastic</a> centre. In 1778, it settled permanently at its present location, the junction of the <a href="/wiki/Tuul_River" title="Tuul River">Tuul</a> and Selbe rivers. Before that, it changed location twenty-eight times, with each location being chosen ceremonially. In the twentieth century, Ulaanbaatar grew into a major manufacturing centre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Official-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names_and_etymology"><span id="Names_and_etymology"></span>Names and etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names and etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Names_of_Ulaanbaatar_in_different_languages" title="Names of Ulaanbaatar in different languages">Names of Ulaanbaatar in different languages</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:45px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ulaghanbaghatur.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="110" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ulaghanbaghatur.svg/43px-Ulaghanbaghatur.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ulaghanbaghatur.svg/65px-Ulaghanbaghatur.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Ulaghanbaghatur.svg/86px-Ulaghanbaghatur.svg.png 2x" width="43"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ulaghanbaghatur.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Ulaganbagatur</i> in <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_script" title="Mongolian script">classical Mongolian script</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ulaanbaatar has been given numerous names in its history. Before 1911, the official name was <b>Ikh Khüree</b> (<a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a>: <span lang="mn">Их Хүрээ</span>, "Great Settlement") or <b>Daa Khüree</b> (Даа Хүрээ, <i>dà</i>, "great"), or simply <b>Khüree</b>. The Chinese equivalent, <i>Dà kùlún</i> (大庫倫), was rendered into Western languages as "Kulun" or "Kuren."</p>
<p>Upon independence in 1911, with both the secular government and the <a href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan" title="Bogd Khan">Bogd Khan</a>'s palace present, the city's name changed to <i>Niĭslel Khüree</i> (Нийслэл Хүрээ, "Capital Camp"). It is called <b>Bogdiin Khuree</b> (Богдын Хүрээ, <i>Bogdiĭn Khüree</i>, "Great Holy Khan's Monastery") in the folk song "<a href="/wiki/Praise_of_Bogdiin_Khuree" title="Praise of Bogdiin Khuree">Praise of Bogdiin Khuree</a>". In western languages, the city at that time was most often referred to as <b>Urga</b> (from <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a>: <span lang="mn">Өргөө</span>, <i>Örgöö</i>, "Palace").</p>
<p>When the city became the capital of the new <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Republic" title="Mongolian People's Republic">Mongolian People's Republic</a> in 1924, its name was changed to Ulaanbaatar (Улаанбаатар, <i>Ulaanbaatar</i>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_script" title="Mongolian script">classical Mongolian</a> <i>Ulaganbagatur</i>, literally "Red Hero"). On the session of the 1st Great People's Khuraldaan of Mongolia in 1924, a majority of delegates expressed their wish to change the capital city's name to <i><a href="/wiki/Baghatur" title="Baghatur">Baatar</a> Khot</i> ("Hero City"). However, under the pressure of the Soviet activist of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comintern" title="Comintern">Communist International</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turar_Ryskulov" title="Turar Ryskulov">Turar Ryskulov</a>, the city was named <i>Ulaanbaatar Khot</i> ("City of Red Hero").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Europe and North America, Ulaanbaatar continued to be generally known as Urga or Khure until 1924, and Ulan Bator afterwards (a spelling derived from <span lang="ru"><i>Улан-Батор</i></span>, <i>Ulan-Bator</i>). The Russian spelling ("Улан-Батор") is the Russian phonetic equivalent of the Mongolian name, according to Russian spelling conventions. This form was defined two decades before the Mongolian name got its current <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Mongolian Cyrillic alphabet">Cyrillic script</a> spelling and 'Ulaanbaatar' transliteration (1941–1950).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ulaanbaatar" title="History of Ulaanbaatar">History of Ulaanbaatar</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Human habitation at the site of Ulaanbaatar dates from the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a>, with a number of sites on <a href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan_Mountain" title="Bogd Khan Mountain">Bogd Khan Mountain</a>, Buyant-Ukhaa and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Songinokhairkhan_Mountain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Songinokhairkhan Mountain (page does not exist)">Songinokhairkhan Mountain</a> revealing tools dating from 300,000 years ago to 40,000–12,000 years ago. These Upper Paleolithic people hunted <a href="/wiki/Mammoth" title="Mammoth">mammoth</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wooly_rhinoceros" title="Wooly rhinoceros">wooly rhinoceros</a>, the bones of which are found abundantly around Ulaanbaatar.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_1639">Before 1639</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Before 1639">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WangKhanRuins.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="805" data-file-width="1340" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/WangKhanRuins.jpg/220px-WangKhanRuins.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/WangKhanRuins.jpg/330px-WangKhanRuins.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/WangKhanRuins.jpg/440px-WangKhanRuins.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WangKhanRuins.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Remains of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wang_Khan" title="Wang Khan">Wang Khan</a>'s 12th-century palace in Ulaanbaatar</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a> era royal tombs have been discovered around Ulaanbaatar, including the tombs of Belkh Gorge near Dambadarjaalin monastery and tombs of Songinokhairkhan. Located on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Tuul_River" title="Tuul River">Tuul River</a>, Ulaanbaatar has been well within the sphere of Turco-Mongol <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nomadic_empires" title="Nomadic empires">nomadic empires</a> throughout history.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wang_Khan" title="Wang Khan">Wang Khan</a> Toghrul of the <a href="/wiki/Keraites" title="Keraites">Keraites</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_East" title="Church of the East">Nestorian Christian</a> monarch whom <a href="/wiki/Marco_Polo" title="Marco Polo">Marco Polo</a> identified as the legendary <a href="/wiki/Prester_John" title="Prester John">Prester John</a>, is said to have had his palace here (the Black Forest of the Tuul River) and forbade hunting in the holy mountain Bogd Uul. The palace is said to be where <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a> stayed with <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Yesui_Khatun&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Yesui Khatun (page does not exist)">Yesui Khatun</a> before attacking the <a href="/wiki/Tangut_people" title="Tangut people">Tangut</a> in 1226.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_monastery">Mobile monastery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mobile monastery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Founded in 1639 as a <a href="/wiki/Yurt" title="Yurt">yurt</a> monastery, Ulaanbaatar, originally <b>Örgöö</b> (palace-<a href="/wiki/Yurt" title="Yurt">yurt</a>), was first located at Lake Shireet Tsagaan nuur (75 kilometres (47 miles) directly east of the imperial capital <a href="/wiki/Karakorum" title="Karakorum">Karakorum</a>) in what is now <a href="/wiki/B%C3%BCrd,_%C3%96v%C3%B6rkhangai" title="Bürd, Övörkhangai">Burd sum</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%96v%C3%B6rkhangai_Province" title="Övörkhangai Province">Övörkhangai</a>, around 230 kilometres (143 miles) south-west from the present site of Ulaanbaatar, and was intended by the Mongol nobles to be the seat of the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jebtsundamba_Khutughtu" title="Jebtsundamba Khutughtu">Jebtsundamba Khutughtu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zanabazar" title="Zanabazar">Zanabazar</a>. In 1651 Zanabazar returned to Mongolia from Tibet and founded seven <i>aimags</i> (monastic departments) in Urga, later establishing four more.</p>
<p>As a mobile monastery-town, it was often moved to various places along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Selenga" title="Selenga">Selenge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orkhon_River" title="Orkhon River">Orkhon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuul_River" title="Tuul River">Tuul</a> rivers, as supply and other needs would demand. During the <a href="/wiki/Dzungar_Khanate" title="Dzungar Khanate">Dzungar</a> wars of the late 17th century, it was even moved to <a href="/wiki/Inner_Mongolia" title="Inner Mongolia">Inner Mongolia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> As the city grew, it moved less and less.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BH_of_UB_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-BH_of_UB-6">[6]</a></sup> The movements of the city can be detailed as following: Shireet Tsagaan Nuur (1639), Khoshoo Tsaidam (1640), Khentii Mountains (1654), Ogoomor (1688), Inner Mongolia (1690), Tsetserlegiin Erdene Tolgoi (1700), Daagandel (1719), Usan Seer (1720), Ikh Tamir (1722), Jargalant (1723), Eeven Gol (1724), Khujirtbulan (1729), Burgaltai (1730), Sognogor (1732), Terelj (1733), Uliastai River (1734), Khui Mandal (1736), Khuntsal (1740), Udleg (1742), Ogoomor (1743), Selbe (1747), Uliastai River (1756), Selbe (1762), Khui Mandal (1772) and Selbe (1778).</p>
<p>In 1778, the city moved from Khui Mandal and settled for good at its current location, near the confluence of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Selbe_Gol&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Selbe Gol (page does not exist)">Selbe</a> and Tuul rivers and beneath <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan_Uul" title="Bogd Khan Uul">Bogd Khan Uul</a>, back then also on the caravan route from <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kyakhta" title="Kyakhta">Kyakhta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> One of the earliest Western mentions of Urga is the account of the Scottish traveller <a href="/wiki/John_Bell_(traveller)" title="John Bell (traveller)">John Bell</a> in 1721:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>What they call the Urga is the court, or the place where the prince (Tusheet Khan) and high priest (Bogd Jebtsundamba Khutugtu) reside, who are always encamped at no great distance from one another. They have several thousand tents about them, which are removed from time to time. The Urga is much frequented by merchants from China and Russia, and other places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>By Zanabazar's death in 1723, Urga was the Mongolia's preeminent monastery in terms of religious authority. A council of seven of the highest ranking lamas (<i>Khamba Nomon Khan</i>, <i>Ded Khamba</i> and five <i>Tsorj</i>) made most of the city's religious decisions. It had also become Outer Mongolia's commercial center. From 1733 to 1778, Urga moved in the vicinity of its present location. In 1754, the Erdene Shanzodba Yam <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_Administration_of_Ecclesiastical_Estate"><b><a href="#ref_Administration_of_Ecclesiastical_Estate">^</a></b></span> of Urga was given authority to supervise the administrative affairs of the Bogd's subjects. It also served as the city's chief judicial court. In 1758 the Qianlong Emperor appointed the Khalkha Vice General Sanzaidorj as the first Mongol amban of Urga with full authority to "oversee the Khuree and administer well all the Khutugtu's subjects".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In 1761, a second amban was appointed for the same purpose, a Manchu one.</p>
<p>In 1786, a decree issued in Peking gave right to the Urga ambans to decide the administrative affairs of Tusheet Khan and Setsen Khan territories. With this, Urga became the highest civil authority in the country. Based on Urga's Mongol governor Sanzaidorj's petition, the <a href="/wiki/Qianlong_Emperor" title="Qianlong Emperor">Qianlong Emperor</a> officially recognized an annual ceremony on Bogd Khan Mountain in 1778 and provided the annual imperial donations. The city was the seat of the Jebtsundamba Khutugtus, two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing</a> <a href="/wiki/Amban" title="Amban">ambans</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a> trade town grew "four trees" or 4.24 km (2.63 mi) east of the city center at the confluence of the Uliastai and Tuul rivers.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OldPaintingUrga.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1043" data-file-width="1391" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/OldPaintingUrga.jpg/260px-OldPaintingUrga.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/OldPaintingUrga.jpg/390px-OldPaintingUrga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/OldPaintingUrga.jpg/520px-OldPaintingUrga.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OldPaintingUrga.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Detail of 19th-century painting of Urga (Ulaanbaatar): in the centre the movable square temple of Bat Tsagaan, built in 1654, besides numerous other temples</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By 1778, Urga may have had around ten thousand monks. They were regulated by a monastic rule called the Internal Rule of the Grand Monastery or <i>Yeke Kuriyen-u Doto'adu Durem</i> (for example, in 1797 a decree of the 4th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jebtsundamba" title="Jebtsundamba">Jebtsundamba</a> forbade "singing, playing with archery, myagman, chess, usury and smoking"). Executions were forbidden where the holy temples of the Bogd Jebtsundama could be seen, so capital punishment took place away from the city. In 1839, the 5th Bogd Jebtsundamba moved his residence to Gandan Hill, an elevated position to the west of the Baruun Damnuurchin markets. Part of the city was moved to nearby Tolgoit. In 1855 the part of the camp that moved to Tolgoit was brought back to its 1778 location and the 7th Bogd Jebtsundamba returned to the Zuun Khuree. The Gandan Monastery flourished as a center of philosophical studies.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Consulate_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_Urgoo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="421" data-file-width="726" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Consulate_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_Urgoo.jpg/260px-Consulate_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_Urgoo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Consulate_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_Urgoo.jpg/390px-Consulate_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_Urgoo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Consulate_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_Urgoo.jpg/520px-Consulate_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_Urgoo.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Consulate_of_the_Russian_Empire_in_Urgoo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Russian Consulate of Urga (Ulaanbaatar) and the Holy Trinity Church, both built in 1863</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urga_and_the_Kyakhta_trade">Urga and the Kyakhta trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Urga and the Kyakhta trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kyakhta" title="Treaty of Kyakhta">Treaty of Kyakhta</a> in 1727 Urga (Ulaanbaatar) was a major point of the <a href="/wiki/Kyakhta_trade" title="Kyakhta trade">Kyakhta trade</a> between Russia and China – mostly Siberian furs for Chinese cloth and later tea. The route ran south to Urga, southeast across the Gobi to Kalgan and southeast over the mountains to Peking. Urga was also a collection point for goods coming from further west. These were either sent to China or shipped north to Russia via Kyakhta because of legal restrictions and the lack of good trade routes to the west.</p>
<p>By 1908<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> there was a Russian quarter with a few hundred merchants and a Russian club and informal Russian mayor. East of the main town was the Russian consulate built in 1863 with an Orthodox church, post office and 20 Cossack guards. It was fortified in 1900 and briefly occupied by troops during the Boxer Rebellion. There was a telegraph line north to Kyakhta and southeast to Kalgan and weekly postal service along these routes. Beyond the Russian consulate was the Chinese trading post called Maimaicheng and nearby the palace of the Manchu viceroy. With the growth of Western trade at the Chinese ports the tea trade to Russia declined,some Chinese merchants left and wool became the main export. Manufactured goods still came from Russia but most were now brought from Kalgan by caravan. The annual trade was estimated at 25 million rubles, nine tenths in Chinese hands and one tenth Russian.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:662px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A3%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0,_1891.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1832" data-file-width="6214" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/%D0%A3%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0%2C_1891.jpg/660px-%D0%A3%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0%2C_1891.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/%D0%A3%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0%2C_1891.jpg/990px-%D0%A3%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0%2C_1891.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/%D0%A3%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0%2C_1891.jpg/1320px-%D0%A3%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0%2C_1891.jpg 2x" width="660"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A3%D1%80%D0%B3%D0%B0,_1891.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Engraving of N.A.Charushin's panorama photo of the old center of Urga from trip (1888) with <a href="/wiki/Grigory_Potanin" title="Grigory Potanin">Potanin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:662px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jugder3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="737" data-file-width="1406" height="346" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Jugder3.jpg/660px-Jugder3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Jugder3.jpg/990px-Jugder3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Jugder3.jpg/1320px-Jugder3.jpg 2x" width="660"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jugder3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A 1913 panorama of Urga. The large circular compound in the middle is the Zuun Khuree temple-palace complex. The Gandan temple complex is to the left. The palaces of the Bogd are to the south of the river. To the far bottom right of the painting is the Maimaicheng district. To its left are the white buildings of the Russian consulate area. The Manjusri monastery can be seen on Mount Bogd Khan Uul at the bottom-right of the painting</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_socialist_era">Independence and socialist era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Independence and socialist era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Duo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="554" data-file-width="353" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Duo.jpg/170px-San_Duo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Duo.jpg/255px-San_Duo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/San_Duo.jpg/340px-San_Duo.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Duo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sānduō (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>: <span lang="zh">三多</span>), an ethnic Mongol, was the 62nd and last <a href="/wiki/Amban" title="Amban">Qing Amban</a> (1910–1911) of Urga.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Moscow trade expedition of the 1910s estimated the population of Urga at 60,000 based on <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Przhevalsky" title="Nikolay Przhevalsky">Nikolay Przhevalsky</a>'s study in the 1870s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archives.gov.mn_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-archives.gov.mn-11">[11]</a></sup> The city's population swelled during the Naadam festival and major religious festivals to more than 100,000. In 1919 the number of monks had reached 20,000, up from 13,000 in 1810.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archives.gov.mn_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-archives.gov.mn-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1910 the <i>amban</i> Sando went to quell a major fight between Gandan lamas and Chinese traders started by an incident at the Da Yi Yu shop in the Baruun Damnuurchin market district. He was unable to bring the lamas under control and was forced to flee back to his quarters. In 1911, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qing_Dynasty" title="Qing Dynasty">Qing Dynasty</a> in China headed for total collapse, Mongolian leaders in Ikh Khüree for <a href="/wiki/Naadam" title="Naadam">Naadam</a> met in secret on Mount Bogd Khan Uul and resolved to end 220 years of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchu" title="Manchu">Manchu</a> control of their country.</p>
<p>On December 29, 1911 the <a href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan" title="Bogd Khan">8th Jeptsundamba Khutughtu</a> was declared ruler of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Outer_Mongolia_(1911%E2%80%931919)" title="Outer Mongolia (1911–1919)">independent Mongolia</a> and assumed the title Bogd Khan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BH_of_UB_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-BH_of_UB-6">[6]</a></sup> Khüree as the seat of the Jebtsundamba Khutugtu was the logical choice for the capital of the new state. However, in the tripartite Kyakhta agreement of 1915 (between Russia, China, Mongolia), Mongolia's status was changed to mere autonomy. In 1919, Mongolian nobles, over the opposition of the Bogd Khan, agreed with the Chinese resident Chen Yi on a settlement of the "Mongolian question" along Qing-era lines, but before this settlement could be put into effect, Khüree was occupied by the troops of Chinese warlord <a href="/wiki/Xu_Shuzheng" title="Xu Shuzheng">Xu Shuzheng</a>, who forced the Mongolian nobles and clergy to renounce autonomy completely.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1913_in_Khuree.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1913_in_Khuree.jpg/220px-1913_in_Khuree.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1913_in_Khuree.jpg/330px-1913_in_Khuree.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1913_in_Khuree.jpg/440px-1913_in_Khuree.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1913_in_Khuree.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1913 color photo of Gandan Monastery</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1921 the city changed hands twice. First, on February 4, 1921, a mixed Russian/Mongolian force led by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_Movement" title="White Movement">White Russian</a> warlord <a href="/wiki/Roman_von_Ungern-Sternberg" title="Roman von Ungern-Sternberg">Roman von Ungern-Sternberg</a> captured the city, freeing the <a href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan" title="Bogd Khan">Bogd Khan</a> from Chinese imprisonment and killing a part of the Chinese garrison. Baron Ungern's capture of Urga was followed by clearing out Mongolia's small gangs of demoralized Chinese soldiers and, at the same time, looting and murder of foreigners, including a vicious pogrom that killed off the <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-By_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-By-14">[14]</a></sup> Jewish community. On February 22, 1921 the Bogd Khan was once again elevated the Great Khan of Mongolia in Urga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> However, at the same time Baron Ungern was taking control of Urga, a Soviet-supported Communist Mongolian force led by <a href="/wiki/Damdin_S%C3%BCkhbaatar" title="Damdin Sükhbaatar">Damdin Sükhbaatar</a> was forming up in Russia, and in March they crossed the border. Ungern and his men rode out in May to meet Red Russian and Red Mongolian troops, but suffered a disastrous defeat in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In July the Communist Soviet-Mongolian army became the second conquering force in six months to enter Urga. Mongolia came to the control of the Soviet Russia. On October 29, 1924 the town was renamed to Ulaanbaatar (Mongolian "red hero"), by the advice of T.R. Ryskulov, the Soviet representative in Mongolia.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dzah.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="876" data-file-width="1331" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Dzah.jpg/220px-Dzah.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Dzah.jpg/330px-Dzah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Dzah.jpg/440px-Dzah.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dzah.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Outdoor market near Gandan hill in 1972; State Department Store in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FoliageUB7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="851" data-file-width="1134" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/FoliageUB7.jpg/220px-FoliageUB7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/FoliageUB7.jpg/330px-FoliageUB7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/FoliageUB7.jpg/440px-FoliageUB7.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FoliageUB7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Green areas were increased in the city center during the communist era.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the socialist period, especially following the Second World War, most of the old <a href="/wiki/Ger_district" title="Ger district">ger districts</a> were replaced by <a href="/wiki/Ugsarmal_bair" title="Ugsarmal bair">Soviet-style blocks of flats</a>, often financed by the Soviet Union. <a href="/wiki/Urban_planning" title="Urban planning">Urban planning</a> began in the 1950s and most of the city today is the result of construction from 1960 to 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transmongolian_Railway" title="Transmongolian Railway">Transmongolian Railway</a>, connecting Ulaanbaatar with Moscow and Beijing, was completed in 1956 and cinemas, theaters, museums etc. were erected. On the other hand, most of the temples and monasteries of pre-socialist Khüree were destroyed following the anti-religious <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stalinist_purges_in_Mongolia" title="Stalinist purges in Mongolia">purges</a> of the late 1930s. The Gandan monastery was reopened in 1944 when the <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">U.S. Vice President</a> <a href="/wiki/Henry_A._Wallace" title="Henry A. Wallace">Henry Wallace</a> asked to see a monastery during his visit to Mongolia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Democratic_protests_of_1989.E2.80.931990">Democratic protests of 1989–1990</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Democratic protests of 1989–1990">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ulaanbaatar was the site of demonstrations that led to Mongolia's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1990_Democratic_Revolution_in_Mongolia" title="1990 Democratic Revolution in Mongolia">transition to democracy and market economy in 1990</a>. On December 10, 1989, protesters outside the Youth Culture Centre called for Mongolia to implement <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a> in their full sense. Dissident leaders demanded free elections and economic reform. On January 14, 1990 the protesters, having grown from two hundred to over a thousand, met at the Lenin Museum in Ulaanbaatar. A demonstration in Sükhbaatar Square on Jan. 21 followed. Afterwards, weekend demonstrations in January and February were held accompanied by the forming of Mongolia's first opposition parties. On March 7, ten dissidents assembled in Sükhbaatar Square and went on a hunger strike. Thousands of supporters joined them. More came on March 8, and the crowd grew more unruly; seventy people were injured and one killed. On March 9 the communist <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Party" title="Mongolian People's Party">Mongolian People's Revolutionary Party</a> government resigned. The provisional government announced Mongolia's first free elections, which were held in July. The <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Party" title="Mongolian People's Party">MPRP</a> won the election and resumed power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_1990">Since 1990</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Since 1990">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since Mongolia's transition to a market economy in 1990, the city has experienced further growth – especially in the ger districts, as construction of new blocks of flats had basically broken down in the 1990s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The population has more than doubled to over one million inhabitants. This causes a number of social, environmental, and transportation problems. In recent years, construction of new buildings has gained new momentum, especially in the city center, and apartment prices have skyrocketed.</p>
<p>In 2008, Ulaanbaatar was the scene of riots after the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Mongolia)" title="Democratic Party (Mongolia)">Mongolian Democratic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civic_Will_Party" title="Civic Will Party">Civic Will Party</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(Mongolia)" title="Republican Party (Mongolia)">Republican</a> parties disputed the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Party" title="Mongolian People's Party">Mongolian People's Revolutionary Party</a>'s victory in the <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_legislative_election,_2008" title="Mongolian legislative election, 2008">parliamentary elections</a>. A four-day state of emergency was declared, the capital was placed under a 22:00 to 08:00 curfew, and alcohol sales banned,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC2_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2-19">[19]</a></sup> following which measures rioting did not resume.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC3_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC3-20">[20]</a></sup> This was the first deadly riot in modern Ulaanbaatar's history.</p>
<p>In April 2013 Ulaanbaatar hosted the 7th Ministerial Conference of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Democracies" title="Community of Democracies">Community of Democracies</a>, and has also lent its name to the Ulaanbaatar Dialogue on Northeast Asian Security.</p>
<p>Since July 7, 2016, the Mayor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulanbataar" title="Ulanbataar">Ulanbataar</a> and Governor of the Capital City is <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCkhbaataryn_Batbold" title="Sükhbaataryn Batbold">Sükhbaataryn Batbold</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mayor_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-mayor-21">[21]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Mongolian_People%27s_Party" title="Mongolian People's Party">Mongolian People's Party</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ulaanbaatar is located at about 1,350 metres (4,430 ft) above mean <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>, slightly east of the centre of Mongolia on the <a href="/wiki/Tuul_River" title="Tuul River">Tuul River</a>, a sub<a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributary</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Selenga" title="Selenga">Selenge</a>, in a valley at the foot of the mountain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan_Uul" title="Bogd Khan Uul">Bogd Khan Uul</a>. Bogd Khan Uul is a broad, heavily forested mountain rising 2,250 metres (7,380 ft) to the south of Ulaanbaatar. It forms the boundary between the <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> zone to the south and the forest-steppe zone to the north.</p>
<p>It is also one of the oldest reserves in the world, being protected by law since the 18th century. The forests of the mountains surrounding Ulaanbaatar are composed of evergreen pines, <a href="/wiki/Deciduous" title="Deciduous">deciduous</a> larches and <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">birches</a> while the riverine forest of the Tuul River is composed of broad-leaved, deciduous <a href="/wiki/Populus" title="Populus">poplars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elm" title="Elm">elms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Willow" title="Willow">willows</a>. As a point of reference Ulaanbaatar lies on roughly the same latitude as <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Orléans">Orléans</a>. It lies on roughly the same longitude as <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>.</p>
<p>Owing to its high elevation, its relatively high latitude, its location hundreds of kilometres from any coast, and the effects of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siberian_anticyclone" title="Siberian anticyclone">Siberian anticyclone</a>, Ulaanbaatar is the coldest national capital in the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montsame_News_Agency_2006.2C_p._35_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Montsame_News_Agency_2006.2C_p._35-22">[22]</a></sup> with a <a href="/wiki/Monsoon" title="Monsoon">monsoon</a>-influenced, cold <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" title="Cold semi-arid climate">BSk</a></i>, USDA <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">Plant Hardiness Zone</a> 3b<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>) that closely borders a <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a> (<i>Dwc</i>) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warm-summer_humid_continental" title="Warm-summer humid continental">warm-summer humid continental</a> (<i>Dwb</i>).</p>
<p>The city features brief, warm summers and long, bitterly cold and dry winters. The coldest January temperatures, usually at the time just before sunrise, are between −36 and −40 °C (−32.8 and −40.0 °F) with no wind, due to temperature inversion. Most of the annual <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> of 267 millimetres (10.51 in) falls from June to September. The highest recorded precipitation in the city was 659 millimetres or 25.94 inches at the Khureltogoot Astronomical Observatory on Mount Bogd Khan Uul. Ulaanbaatar has an average annual temperature of −0.4 °C or 31.3 °F,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HKO_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-HKO-24">[24]</a></sup> making it the coldest capital in the world.</p>
<p>The city lies in the zone of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discontinuous_permafrost" title="Discontinuous permafrost">discontinuous permafrost</a>, which means that building is difficult in sheltered aspects that preclude thawing in the summer, but easier on more exposed ones where soils fully thaw. Suburban residents live in traditional <a href="/wiki/Yurt" title="Yurt">yurts</a> that do not protrude into the soil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Extreme temperatures in the city range from −42.2 °C (−44.0 °F) in January and February 1957 to 39.0 °C (102.2 °F) in July 1988.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pogoda_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-pogoda-26">[26]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Panoramas">Panoramas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Panoramas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1358px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UBpanaroma2.jpg" title="from  Zaisan Memorial in 2013."><img alt="" data-file-height="246" data-file-width="1350" height="246" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/80/UBpanaroma2.jpg" width="1350"/></a></div>

<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UBpanaroma2.jpg" title="File:UBpanaroma2.jpg"></a></div>
from <a href="/wiki/Zaisan_Memorial" title="Zaisan Memorial">Zaisan Memorial</a> in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration_and_subdivisions">Administration and subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administration and subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C3%BC%C3%BCreg" title="Düüreg">Düüreg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ulan_Bator_subdivisions.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1545" data-file-width="2311" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ulan_Bator_subdivisions.png/260px-Ulan_Bator_subdivisions.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ulan_Bator_subdivisions.png/390px-Ulan_Bator_subdivisions.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Ulan_Bator_subdivisions.png/520px-Ulan_Bator_subdivisions.png 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ulan_Bator_subdivisions.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the districts of Ulaanbaatar</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ulaanbaatar is divided into nine districts (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C3%BC%C3%BCreg" title="Düüreg">Düüregs</a>): <a href="/wiki/Baganuur" title="Baganuur">Baganuur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bagakhangai" title="Bagakhangai">Bagakhangai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayangol,_Ulaanbaatar" title="Bayangol, Ulaanbaatar">Bayangol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bayanz%C3%BCrkh" title="Bayanzürkh">Bayanzürkh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chingeltei" title="Chingeltei">Chingeltei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khan_Uul" title="Khan Uul">Khan Uul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nalaikh" title="Nalaikh">Nalaikh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Songino_Khairkhan" title="Songino Khairkhan">Songino Khairkhan</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCkhbaatar_(district)" title="Sükhbaatar (district)">Sükhbaatar</a>. Each district is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Khoroo" title="Khoroo">khoroos</a>, of which there are 121.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montsame_News_Agency_2006.2C_p._35_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Montsame_News_Agency_2006.2C_p._35-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>The capital is governed by a city council (the Citizen's Representatives Hural) with forty members, elected every four years. The city council appoints the mayor. When his predecessor became prime minister in January 2006, former city manager Gombosuren Monkhbayar was elected mayor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Ulaanbaatar is governed as an independent first-level region, separate from the surrounding <a href="/wiki/T%C3%B6v_Province" title="Töv Province">Töv Aimag</a>.</p>
<p>The city consists of a central district built in Soviet 1940s and 1950s-style architecture, surrounded by and mingled with residential concrete towerblocks and large ger districts. In recent years, many of the towerblock's ground floors have been modified and upgraded to small shops, and many new buildings have been erected, some of them illegally (some private companies erect buildings without the legal licenses or in forbidden places).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As the main industrial center of <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>, Ulaanbaatar produces a variety of consumer goods <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and is responsible for about two-thirds of Mongolia's total gross domestic product (GDP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-30">[30]</a></sup> The transition into a market economy in 1990, which has led to a shift towards service industries making up 43% of the city's GDP, along with rapid urbanization and population growth has so far correlated with an increase in GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mining makes up the second largest contributor to Ulaanbaatar's GDP at 25%. North of the city are several gold mines, including the <a href="/wiki/Boroo_Gold_Mine" title="Boroo Gold Mine">Boroo Gold Mine</a>, and foreign investment in the sector has allowed for growth and development. However, in light of a noticeable drop in GDP during the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">Financial Crisis of 2008</a> as demand for mining exports dropped,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-31">[31]</a></sup> there has been movement towards diversifying the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sights">Sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mainstream tourist guide books usually recommend the <a href="/wiki/Gandantegchinlen_Monastery" title="Gandantegchinlen Monastery">Gandantegchinlen Monastery</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> with the large Janraisig statue, the socialist monument complex at <a href="/wiki/Zaisan_Memorial" title="Zaisan Memorial">Zaisan Memorial</a> with its great view over the city, the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace_of_the_Bogd_Khan" title="Winter Palace of the Bogd Khan">Winter Palace of the Bogd Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinggis_Square" title="Chinggis Square">Chinggis Square</a> and the nearby <a href="/wiki/Choijin_Lama_Temple" title="Choijin Lama Temple">Choijin Lama Temple</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Additionally, Ulaanbaatar houses numerous museums, two of the prominent ones being the National Museum of Mongolia and the Zanabazar Fine Arts Museum. Popular destinations for day trips are the <a href="/wiki/Gorkhi-Terelj_National_Park" title="Gorkhi-Terelj National Park">Gorkhi-Terelj National Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Manjusri_Monastery" title="Manjusri Monastery">Manzushir monastery</a> ruins on the southern flank of Bogd Khan Uul and <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan_Equestrian_Statue" title="Genghis Khan Equestrian Statue">Genghis Khan Equestrian Statue</a>.</p>
<p>Important shopping districts include the 3rd Microdistrict Boulevard (simply called <i>Khoroolol</i> or "the District"), Peace Avenue around the State Department Store (simply called <i>Ikh Delguur</i> or "Great Store") and the Narantuul "Black Market" area (simply called <i>Zakh</i> or "the Market"). Ulaanbaatar presently has three large cinemas, one modern ski resort, two large indoor stadiums, several large department stores and one large amusement park. Food, entertainment and recreation venues are steadily increasing in variety. <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Round_Table_Pizza" title="Round Table Pizza">Round Table Pizza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinnabon" title="Cinnabon">Cinnabon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramada" title="Ramada">Ramada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kempinski" title="Kempinski">Kempinski</a> have opened branches in key locations.</p>
<p>A 309-metre-tall (1,014-foot) tower called the Morin Khuur Tower (Horsehead Fiddle Tower) is planned to be built next to the Central Stadium. It is scheduled to finish in 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Other future skyscrapers are the 34-floor Shangri-La Phase 2 luxury hotel project (construction ongoing and scheduled to finish in 2015)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and the 41-floor Mak Tower being built by South Korean "Lotte Construction and Engineering".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monasteries">Monasteries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Monasteries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Among the notable older monasteries is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Choijin_Lama_Monastery" title="Choijin Lama Monastery">Choijin Lama Monastery</a>, a Buddhist monastery that was completed in 1908. It escaped the destruction of Mongolian monasteries when it was turned into a museum in 1942.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Another is the <a href="/wiki/Gandantegchinlen_Monastery" title="Gandantegchinlen Monastery">Gandan Monastery</a>, which dates to the 19th century. Its most famous attraction is a 26.5-meter-high golden statue of <a href="/wiki/Avalokite%C5%9Bvara" title="Avalokiteśvara">Migjid Janraisig</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> These monasteries are among the very few in Mongolia to escape the wholesale destruction of Mongolian monasteries under <a href="/wiki/Khorloogiin_Choibalsan" title="Khorloogiin Choibalsan">Khorloogiin Choibalsan</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Winter_Palace">Winter Palace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Winter Palace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Winter_Palace_Bogd_Khan_149185394_bfcc8db25b_b.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1967" data-file-width="2965" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Winter_Palace_Bogd_Khan_149185394_bfcc8db25b_b.jpg/260px-Winter_Palace_Bogd_Khan_149185394_bfcc8db25b_b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Winter_Palace_Bogd_Khan_149185394_bfcc8db25b_b.jpg/390px-Winter_Palace_Bogd_Khan_149185394_bfcc8db25b_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Winter_Palace_Bogd_Khan_149185394_bfcc8db25b_b.jpg/520px-Winter_Palace_Bogd_Khan_149185394_bfcc8db25b_b.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Winter_Palace_Bogd_Khan_149185394_bfcc8db25b_b.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Peace Gate of the Winter Palace (<i>Amgalan Enkhiin Khaalga</i> in Mongolian, <i>Andimen</i> in Chinese), for which no nails were used</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Old Ikh Khüree, once the city was set up as a permanent capital, had a number of palaces and noble residences in an area called <i>Öndgiin sürgiin nutag</i>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jebtsundamba_Khutughtu" title="Jebtsundamba Khutughtu">Jebtsundamba Khutughtu</a>, who was later crowned <a href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan" title="Bogd Khan">Bogd Khan</a>, had four main imperial residences, which were located between the Middle (<i>Dund gol</i>) and Tuul rivers. The summer palace was called <i>Erdmiin dalai buyan chuulgan süm</i> or <i>Bogd khaanii serüün ord</i>. Other palaces were the White palace (<i>Tsagaan süm</i> or <i>Gьngaa dejidlin</i>), and the Pandelin palace (also called <i><a href="/wiki/Narodakini" title="Narodakini">Naro Kha Chod</a> süm</i>), which was situated in the left bank of Tuul River. Some of the palaces were also used for religious purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The only palace that remains is the winter palace; the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Palace_of_the_Bogd_Khan" title="Winter Palace of the Bogd Khan">Winter Palace of the Bogd Khan</a> (<i>Bogd khaanii nogoon süm</i> or <i>Bogd khaanii öwliin ordon</i>) remains as a museum of the last monarch. The complex includes six temples, many of the Bogd Khan's and his wife's possessions are on display in the main building.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Mongolia" title="List of museums in Mongolia">List of museums in Mongolia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bogd_Khan_Palace_19.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1872" data-file-width="3328" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Bogd_Khan_Palace_19.JPG/220px-Bogd_Khan_Palace_19.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Bogd_Khan_Palace_19.JPG/330px-Bogd_Khan_Palace_19.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Bogd_Khan_Palace_19.JPG/440px-Bogd_Khan_Palace_19.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bogd_Khan_Palace_19.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Throne given to <a href="/wiki/Zanabazar" title="Zanabazar">Zanabazar</a> by his disciple the <a href="/wiki/Kangxi_Emperor" title="Kangxi Emperor">Kangxi Emperor</a>, used by later <a href="/wiki/Jebtsundamba_Khutuktu" title="Jebtsundamba Khutuktu">Jebtsundamba Khutuktus</a> in Urga</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ulaanbaatar has several museums dedicated to Mongolian history and culture. The Natural History Museum features many dinosaur fossils and meteorites found in Mongolia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Mongolia" title="National Museum of Mongolia">National Museum of Mongolia</a> includes exhibits from prehistoric times through the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> to the present.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Zanabazar" title="Zanabazar">Zanabazar</a> Museum of Fine Arts has a large collection of Mongolian art, including works of the 17th-century sculptor/artist Zanabazar, as well as Mongolia's most famous painting, <i>One Day In Mongolia</i> by <a href="/wiki/Marzan_Sharav" title="Marzan Sharav">B. Sharav</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_Theatre_Museum" title="Mongolian Theatre Museum">Mongolian Theatre Museum</a> presents the history of the performing arts in Mongolia. The city's former Lenin Museum announced plans in January 2013 to convert to a museum showcasing dinosaur and other prehistoric fossils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pre-1778 artifacts that never left the city since its founding include the Vajradhara statue made by Zanabazar himself in 1683 (the city's main deity kept at the Vajradhara temple), an ornate throne presented to Zanabazar by the Kangxi Emperor (before 1723), a sandalwood hat presented to Zanabazar by the Dalai Lama (c. 1663), Zanabazar's large fur coat which was also presented by the Kangxi Emperor and a great number of original statues made by Zanabazar (e.g., the Green Tara).</p>
<p>The Military Museum of Mongolia's collection consists of two permanent exhibition halls, showcasing the war history of the country from pre-historic times to the modern era. In the first hall, one can see various tools and weapons from Paleolithic age to the times of Manchu empire. The modern history exhibition hall showcases the history of the Mongolian military, starting with the Bogd Khan period /1911¬-1924/ up to Mongolia’s recent military involvement in peacekeeping operations.</p>
<p>Although the building's condition is dire, the Victims of Political Persecution Memorial Museum tells about one of the most tragic history of Mongolia's 20th century. It is dedicated to those fallen under the political purge that took the lives of over 32,000 statesmen, herders, scholars, politicians and lamas.</p>
<p>The Ulaanbaatar City Museum offers a brief but insightful view of Ulaanbaatar’s history through old maps and photos. The most interesting item is a huge painting of the capital as it looked in 1912 that shows major landmarks such as Gandan Monastery and the Winter Palace of the Bogd Khan. Part of the museum is dedicated to special photo exhibits that change frequently. Mongolian Railway History Museum is an open-air museum that displays 6 types of locomotives used during a 65-year period of Mongolian Railways history.</p>
<p>The Puzzle Toys Museum displays a comprehensive collection of complex wooden toys players can assemble.</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">
<div style="width: 162px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Togchin_temple_ruins_-_Zuunmod_(Mongolia).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Togchin_temple_ruins_-_Zuunmod_%28Mongolia%29.jpg/240px-Togchin_temple_ruins_-_Zuunmod_%28Mongolia%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Togchin_temple_ruins_-_Zuunmod_%28Mongolia%29.jpg/360px-Togchin_temple_ruins_-_Zuunmod_%28Mongolia%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Togchin_temple_ruins_-_Zuunmod_%28Mongolia%29.jpg/480px-Togchin_temple_ruins_-_Zuunmod_%28Mongolia%29.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Ruins of the Tsogchin Temple (1749) of <a href="/wiki/Manjusri_Monastery" title="Manjusri Monastery">Manjusri Monastery</a></p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 110.66666666667px">
