<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinggis_.28S.C3.BCkhbaatar.29_Square">Chinggis (Sükhbaatar) Square</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Chinggis (Sükhbaatar) Square">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UB_downtown.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/UB_downtown.jpg/220px-UB_downtown.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/UB_downtown.jpg/330px-UB_downtown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/UB_downtown.jpg/440px-UB_downtown.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UB_downtown.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Downtown Ulaanbaatar around <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sukhbaatar_Square" title="Sukhbaatar Square">Sukhbaatar Square</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%BCkhbaatar_Square" title="Sükhbaatar Square">Chinggis Square</a>, in the government district, is the center of Ulaanbaatar. The square is 31,068 square metres (334,413 square feet) in size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In the middle of Sükhbaatar Square, there is a statue of <a href="/wiki/Damdin_S%C3%BCkhbaatar" title="Damdin Sükhbaatar">Damdin Sükhbaatar</a> on horseback. The spot was chosen because that was where Sükhbaatar's horse had urinated (a good omen) on July 8, 1921 during a gathering of the Red Army. On the north side of Sükhbaatar Square is the <a href="/wiki/State_Great_Khural" title="State Great Khural">Mongolian Parliament</a> building, featuring a large statue of <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Chinggis Khan</a> at the top of the front steps. Peace Avenue (<i>Enkh Taivny Urgon Chuloo</i>), the main thoroughfare through town, runs along the south side of the square.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zaisan_Memorial">Zaisan Memorial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Zaisan Memorial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Zaisan_Memorial" title="Zaisan Memorial">Zaisan Memorial</a>, a memorial to Soviet soldiers killed in World War II, sits on a hill south of the city. The Zaisan Memorial includes a Soviet tank paid for by the Mongolian people and a circular memorial painting which in the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism" title="Socialist realism">socialist realism</a> style depicts scenes of friendship between the peoples of Soviet Union and Mongolia. Visitors who make the long climb to the top are rewarded with a panoramic view of the whole city down in the valley.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Sport_Stadium">National Sport Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: National Sport Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/National_Sports_Stadium_(Mongolia)" title="National Sports Stadium (Mongolia)">National Sports Stadium</a> is the main sporting venue. The <a href="/wiki/Naadam" title="Naadam">Naadam</a> festival is held here every July.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_culture">Arts and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Arts and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ulaanbaatar features mix of traditional and western style theatres, offering world class performances. Many of the traditional folklore bands play regularly around the world including in New York, London and Tokyo.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Academic_Theatre_of_Opera_and_Ballet_of_Mongolia" title="National Academic Theatre of Opera and Ballet of Mongolia">Ulaanbaatar Opera House</a>, situated in the center of the city, hosts concerts and musical performances. as well as opera and ballet performances, some of them are in collaboration with world ballet houses such as Boston Theatre.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Dance.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/National_Dance.jpg/220px-National_Dance.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/National_Dance.jpg/330px-National_Dance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/National_Dance.jpg/440px-National_Dance.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Dance.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mongolian National Song and Dance Academic Ensemble</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Mongolian State Grand National Orchestra was originally established during <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, reestablished in 1945. It has the largest orchestra of traditional instruments in the country with a repertoire going beyond national music, encompassing dozens of international musical pieces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Tumen Ekh Ensemble comprises artists who perform all types of Mongolian song, music and dance. They play traditional instruments including the <a href="/wiki/Morin_khuur" title="Morin khuur">morin khuur</a> (horse head fiddle) and perform Mongolian long song, epic and eulogy songs, a ritualistic shaman ritual dance, an ancient palace dance and a Tsam mask dance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Morin Khuur Ensemble of Mongolia is part of the Mongolian State Philharmonic located at the Chinggis Khan Square. It is a popular ensemble featuring the national string instrument Morin Khuur and performs various domestic and international works.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GorkhiTereljNationalPark.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/GorkhiTereljNationalPark.jpg/220px-GorkhiTereljNationalPark.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/GorkhiTereljNationalPark.jpg/330px-GorkhiTereljNationalPark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/GorkhiTereljNationalPark.jpg/440px-GorkhiTereljNationalPark.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GorkhiTereljNationalPark.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gorkhi-Terelj_National_Park" title="Gorkhi-Terelj National Park">Gorkhi-Terelj National Park</a> is a popular picnic and camping ground all year round.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">Parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A number of nationally known parks and protected areas belong officially to the city.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gorkhi-Terelj_National_Park" title="Gorkhi-Terelj National Park">Gorkhi-Terelj National Park</a>, a nature preserve with many tourist facilities, is approximately 70 km (43 mi) from Ulaanbaatar. It is accessible via paved road. The 40-metre-high (130-foot) <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan_Equestrian_Statue" title="Genghis Khan Equestrian Statue">Genghis Khan Equestrian Statue</a>, 54 km (34 mi) from Ulaanbaatar, is the largest equestrian statue in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bogd_Khan_mountain" title="Bogd Khan mountain">Bogd Khan mountain</a> is a strictly protected area, with a length of 31 kilometres (19 miles) and width of 3 kilometres (1.9 miles), covering an area of 67,300 hectares (166,302 acres). Nature conservation dates back to the twelfth and thirteenth century when the Toorl Khan of Mongolian Ancient Keraite Aimag – who prohibited logging and hunting activities – claimed the Bogd Khan as a holy mountain. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>National Culture and Recreation Center (Children's Park) is an amusement park located in the downtown section, south of Shangri-La Hotel. It is also a popular place for youngsters to hang out. This small amusement park features rides, games and paddle boats. Its <a href="/wiki/Artificial_Lake_Castle" title="Artificial Lake Castle">Artificial Lake Castle</a> was built in 1969, when the National Amusement Park was established in the centre of the Mongolian capital Ulaanbaatar.</p>
<p>The National Park of Mongolia opened its doors in the southeastern outskirts of the city in 2009, becoming a popular summer park for the UB goers. It has a total area of 55 hectares with over 100K trees planted. The park is geared towards becoming educational center for healthy responsible living as well as environmental education.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Embassies_and_consulates">Embassies and consulates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Embassies and consulates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Street_Cycling.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1201" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Street_Cycling.jpg/220px-Street_Cycling.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Street_Cycling.jpg/330px-Street_Cycling.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Street_Cycling.jpg/440px-Street_Cycling.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Street_Cycling.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Biking event at Peace avenue. Turkish Embassy in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Among the countries that have diplomatic facilities in Ulaanbaatar are Australia, Austria, Bulgaria, Canada, China, Cuba, Czech Republic, Denmark, Finland, France, Germany, India, Japan, Kazakhstan, Laos, Malaysia, Republic of China (Taiwan), Russia, Slovakia, South Korea, Spain, Sweden, Switzerland, Turkey, Ukraine, the United Kingdom, the United States and Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>See above for the temples of Ulaanbaatar's main religion, Buddhism.</p>
<p>It is also the see of the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Prefecture_of_Ulaanbaatar" title="Apostolic Prefecture of Ulaanbaatar">Apostolic Prefecture of Ulaanbaatar</a>, the Roman Catholic missionary circonscription for all (Outer) Mongolia. The apostolic see is the <a href="/wiki/Saints_Peter_and_Paul_Cathedral_(Ulaanbaatar)" title="Saints Peter and Paul Cathedral (Ulaanbaatar)">Saints Peter and Paul Cathedral</a>, consecrated in 2003 from cardinal <a href="/wiki/Crescenzio_Sepe" title="Crescenzio Sepe">Crescenzio Sepe</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_symbols">Municipal symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Municipal symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Naadamceremony2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Naadamceremony2006.jpg/220px-Naadamceremony2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Naadamceremony2006.jpg/330px-Naadamceremony2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Naadamceremony2006.jpg/440px-Naadamceremony2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Naadamceremony2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2006 <a href="/wiki/Naadam" title="Naadam">Naadam</a> ceremony at the National Sports Stadium</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The official symbol of Ulaanbaatar is the <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garu%E1%B8%8Da" title="Garuḍa">garuḍa</a></span>, a mythical bird in both <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> scriptures called <a href="/wiki/Khan_(title)" title="Khan (title)">Khan</a> Garuda or <i>Khangar'd</i> (<a href="/wiki/Mongolian_language" title="Mongolian language">Mongolian</a>: <span lang="mn">Хангарьд</span>) by Mongols.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_emblem">City emblem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: City emblem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garu%E1%B8%8Da" title="Garuḍa">garuḍa</a></span> appears on Ulaanbaatar's <a href="/wiki/Emblem" title="Emblem">emblem</a>. In its right hand is a key, a symbol of prosperity and openness, and in its left is a <a href="/wiki/Nelumbo" title="Nelumbo">lotus</a> flower, a symbol of peace, equality and purity. In its talons it is holding a snake, a symbol of evil of which it is intolerant. On the <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">garuḍa</span>'s forehead is the <a href="/wiki/Soyombo_symbol" title="Soyombo symbol">soyombo symbol</a>, which is featured on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Mongolia" title="Flag of Mongolia">flag of Mongolia</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_flag">City flag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: City flag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city's <a href="/wiki/Flag" title="Flag">flag</a> is sky blue with the <span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="International Alphabet of Sanskrit Transliteration">garuḍa</span> arms in the center.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ulaanbaatar has six major universities:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Mongolia" title="National University of Mongolia">National University of Mongolia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mongolian_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Mongolian University of Science and Technology">Mongolian University of Science and Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mongolian_State_University_of_Agriculture" title="Mongolian State University of Agriculture">Mongolian State University of Agriculture</a></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Health_Science_University_of_Mongolia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Health Science University of Mongolia (page does not exist)">Health Science University of Mongolia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mongolian_State_University_of_Education" title="Mongolian State University of Education">Mongolian State University of Education</a></li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mongolian_University_of_Art_and_Culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mongolian University of Art and Culture (page does not exist)">Mongolian University of Art and Culture</a></li>
</ul>
<p>There are a number of other universities in the city, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humanities_University" title="Humanities University">Humanities University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_of_Finance_and_Economics" title="Institute of Finance and Economics">Institute of Finance and Economics</a> and Raffles International Institute]].<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Mongolia" title="National Library of Mongolia">National Library of Mongolia</a> has a wide selection of English-language texts on Mongolian subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_School_of_Ulaanbaatar" title="American School of Ulaanbaatar">American School of Ulaanbaatar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_School_of_Ulaanbaatar" title="International School of Ulaanbaatar">International School of Ulaanbaatar</a> both offer Western-style K-12 education in English for Mongolian nationals and foreign residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are many public elementary, middle and high schools. In Mongolia, 1–4th grade is elementary, 5–8th is middle and 9-11 is high school. Additionally, there are many private schools that offer bilingual programs.</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mnlibrarypic.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="150" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d2/Mnlibrarypic.jpg" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mnlibrarypic.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The National Library</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Library">National Library</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: National Library">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Mongolia" title="National Library of Mongolia">National Library of Mongolia</a> is located in Ulaanbaatar and includes an extensive historical collection, items in non-Mongolian languages and a special children's collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nla.gov.au_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-nla.gov.au-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_libraries">Public libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Public libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Metropolitan Central Library of Ulaanbaatar, sometimes also referred to as the Ulaanbaatar Public Library, is a <a href="/wiki/Public_library" title="Public library">public library</a> with a collection of about 500,000 items. It has an impressive 232,097 annual users and a total of 497,298 loans per year. It does charge users a registration fee of 3800 to 4250 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tugrik" title="Tugrik">tugrik</a>, or about USD 3.29 to 3.68. The fees may be the result of operating on a budget under $176,000 per year. They also host websites on classical and modern <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_literature" title="Mongolian literature">Mongolian literature</a> and food, in addition to providing free Internet access.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nla.gov.au_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-nla.gov.au-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1986, the Ulaanbaatar government created a centralized system for all public libraries in the city, known as the Metropolitan Library System of Ulaanbaatar (MLSU). This system coordinates management, acquisitions, finances and policy among public libraries in the capital, in addition to providing support to school and children's libraries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Other than the Metropolitan Central Library, the MLSU has four branch libraries. They are in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chingeltei_District" title="Chingeltei District">Chingeltei District</a> (established in 1946), in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Han-Uul_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Han-Uul District (page does not exist)">Han-Uul District</a> (established in 1948), in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bayanzurkh_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bayanzurkh District (page does not exist)">Bayanzurkh District</a> (established in 1968) and in the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Songino-Hairkhan_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Songino-Hairkhan District (page does not exist)">Songino-Hairkhan District</a> (established in 1991). There is also a Children's Central Library, which was established in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_libraries">University libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: University libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>Library of Mongolian State University of Education<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></li>
<li>Library of the Academy of Management<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li>Library of the National University of Mongolia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li>Institutes of the Academy of Sciences (3 department libraries)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
<li>Library of the Institute of Language and Literature<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>Library of the Institute of History<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></li>
<li>Library of the Institute of Finance and Economics<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>Library of the National University of Mongolia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></li>
<li>Library of the Agriculture University</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_libraries">Digital libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Digital libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The International Children's Digital Library (ICDL) is an organization that publishes numerous children's books in different languages on the web in child-friendly formats. In 2006 they began service in Mongolia and have made efforts to provide access to the library in rural areas. The ICDL effort in Mongolia is part of a larger project funded by the World Bank and administered by the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mongolian_Ministry_of_Education,_Culture_and_Science&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mongolian Ministry of Education, Culture and Science (page does not exist)">Mongolian Ministry of Education, Culture and Science</a>, called the Rural Education And Development Project (READ).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Because Mongolia lacks a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publishing_industry" title="Publishing industry">publishing industry</a>, and few children's books, the idea has been to "spur the publishing industry to create 200 new children's books for classroom libraries in grades 1–5." After these books were published and distributed to teachers they were also published online with the rest of the ICDL collection. While a significant portion of this project is supported by outside sources, an important component is to include training of Mongolian staff in order to make it continue in an effective way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The project is also designed to show Mongolia's youth that they can take part in the larger <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_culture" title="Digital culture">digital culture</a>.</p>
<p>The Press Institute in Ulaanbaatar oversees the Digital Archive of Mongolian Newspapers. It is a collection of 45 newspaper titles with a particular focus on the years after the fall of communism in Mongolia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The project was supported by the <a href="/wiki/British_Library" title="British Library">British Library</a>'s <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Endangered_Archives_Programme&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Endangered Archives Programme (page does not exist)">Endangered Archives Programme</a>.</p>
<p>The Metropolitan Central Library in Ulaanbaatar maintains a digital monthly news archive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_libraries">Special libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Special libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An important resource for academics is the American Center for Mongolian Studies (ACMS),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> also based in Ulaanbaatar. Its goal is to facilitate research between Mongolia and the rest of the world and to foster academic partnerships. To help achieve this end, it operates a research library with a reading room and computers for Internet access. ACMS has 1,500 volumes related to Mongolia in numerous languages that may be borrowed with a deposit. It also hosts an online library that includes special reference resources and access to digital databases,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> including a digital book collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a Speaking Library at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Education_for_Blind_and_Visually_Impaired_Students&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Education for Blind and Visually Impaired Students (page does not exist)">School 116 for the visually impaired</a>. This is a project funded by the <a href="/wiki/Zorig_Foundation" title="Zorig Foundation">Zorig Foundation</a>, and the collection is largely based on materials donated by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mongolian_National_Radio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mongolian National Radio (page does not exist)">Mongolian National Radio</a>. "A sizable collection of literature, know-how topics, training materials, music, plays, science broadcasts are now available to the visually impaired at the school."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Mongolia-Japan Center for Human Resources Development<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> maintains a library in Ulaanbaatar consisting of about 7,800 items. The materials in the collection have a strong focus on both aiding Mongolians studying Japanese and books in Japanese about Mongolia. It includes a number of periodicals, textbooks, dictionaries and audio-visual materials. Access to the collection does require payment of a 500 Tugrug fee, though materials are available for loan. They also provide <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Audio-visual_equipment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Audio-visual equipment (page does not exist)">audio-visual equipment</a> for collection use and internet access for an hourly fee. There is also an information retrieval reference service for questions that cannot be answered by their collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archives">Archives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Archives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is a manuscript collection at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Danzan_Ravjaa_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Danzan Ravjaa Museum (page does not exist)">Danzan Ravjaa Museum</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theological" title="Theological">theological</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poetic" title="Poetic">poetic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medicinal" title="Medicinal">medicinal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astrological" title="Astrological">astrological</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theatrical" title="Theatrical">theatrical</a> works. It consists of literature written and collected by the monk <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danzan_Ravjaa" title="Danzan Ravjaa">Danzan Ravjaa</a>, who is famous for his poetry. The British Library's Endangered Archives Programme funded a project to take digital images of unique literature in the collection; however, it is not clear where the images are stored today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ulaanbaatar is served by the <a href="/wiki/Chinggis_Khaan_International_Airport" title="Chinggis Khaan International Airport">Chinggis Khaan International Airport</a> (formerly Buyant Ukhaa Airport). It is 18 km (11 mi) southwest of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Currently, the Chinggis Khaan airport is the only airport in Mongolia that offers international flights. In order to serve increased projected passenger numbers, the <a href="/wiki/New_Ulaanbaatar_International_Airport" title="New Ulaanbaatar International Airport">New Ulaanbaatar International Airport</a> (NUBIA) is being constructed south of the city with plans to replace the Chinggis Khaan airport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Flights to Ulaanbaatar are available from <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, Paris, Frankfurt, Berlin, <a href="/wiki/Ulan-Ude" title="Ulan-Ude">Ulan-Ude</a>, Moscow, <a href="/wiki/Irkutsk" title="Irkutsk">Irkutsk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bishkek" title="Bishkek">Bishkek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> There are rail connections to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_railway" title="Trans-Siberian railway">Trans-Siberian railway</a> via Naushki and to the Chinese railway system via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jining,_Inner_Mongolia" title="Jining, Inner Mongolia">Jining</a>. Ulaanbaatar is connected by road to most of the major towns in Mongolia, but most roads in Mongolia are unpaved and unmarked and road travel can be difficult. Even within the city, not all roads are paved and some of the ones that are paved are not in good condition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Existing plans to improve transportation include several major road projects such as a 1,000-kilometre-long (620-mile) highway to link Ulaanbaatar to the regions of <a href="/wiki/Altanbulag,_Selenge" title="Altanbulag, Selenge">Altanbulag</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zamyn-%C3%9C%C3%BCd" title="Zamyn-Üüd">Zamyn Uud</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> plans to upgrade existing regional airports and roadways, and Mongolian Railway projects that will connect cities and mines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ulaanbaatar-Subway-Plan.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="791" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Ulaanbaatar-Subway-Plan.png/250px-Ulaanbaatar-Subway-Plan.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Ulaanbaatar-Subway-Plan.png/375px-Ulaanbaatar-Subway-Plan.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Ulaanbaatar-Subway-Plan.png/500px-Ulaanbaatar-Subway-Plan.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ulaanbaatar-Subway-Plan.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Planned Ulaanbaatar subway. The central 6.6 km (4.1 mi) will be underground while remaining sections will be elevated.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The national and municipal governments regulate a wide system of private transit providers which operate numerous bus lines around the city. There is also an <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Ulaanbaatar" title="Trolleybuses in Ulaanbaatar">Ulaanbaatar trolleybus system</a>. A secondary transit system of privately owned microbuses (passenger vans) operates alongside these bus lines. Additionally, Ulaanbaatar has over 4000 taxis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The capital has 418.2 km (259.9 mi) of road, of which 76.5 are paved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_pollution">Air pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Air pollution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">Air pollution</a> is a serious problem in Ulaanbaatar, especially in winter. Concentrations of certain types of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Particulate_matter" title="Particulate matter">particulate matter</a> (PM10) regularly exceed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WHO" title="WHO">WHO</a> recommended maximum levels by more than a dozen times. They also exceed the concentrations measured in northern Chinese industrial cities. During the winter months, smoke regularly obscures vision and can even lead to problems with air traffic at the local airport.</p>
<p>Sources of the pollution are mainly the simple stoves used for heating and cooking in the city's <a href="/wiki/Ger_district" title="Ger district">ger districts</a>, but also the local coal-fueled power plants. The problem is compounded by Ulaanbaatar's location in the a valley between relatively high mountains, which shield the city from the winter winds and thus obstruct air circulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ulaanbaatar's residents are very aware of the city's pollution problems (during the winter months, pollution levels and their relation to WHO recommended levels are regularly reported on TV, in a manner similar to weather reports) and ways to amend the situation have been discussed for years; however, no easy solution has been found yet.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ulaanbaatar is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Network_of_Major_Cities_21" title="Asian Network of Major Cities 21">Asian Network of Major Cities 21</a>.</p>

<p>Ulaanbaatar is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Proximity_to_nearby_urban_centers_abroad">Proximity to nearby urban centers abroad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Proximity to nearby urban centers abroad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following is a list of foreign cities close to Ulaanbaatar (UB) sorted by linear distance with additional information on population of each city and linear distance from the Mongolian border. This can be said to be Ulaanbaatar's closest possible sphere of interaction; however, many of these links are not well developed and Ulaanbaatar has closer ties to cities like Seoul (1,995 kilometres or 1,240 miles from UB), Hong Kong (2,900 kilometres or 1,800 miles from UB), Tokyo (3,010 kilometres or 1,870 miles from UB) and Moscow (4,650 kilometres or 2,890 miles from UB). The <a href="/wiki/Zamyn-%C3%9C%C3%BCd" title="Zamyn-Üüd">Zamyn Uud</a>-<a href="/wiki/Erenhot" title="Erenhot">Erenhot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Altanbulag,_Selenge" title="Altanbulag, Selenge">Altanbulag</a>-<a href="/wiki/Kyakhta" title="Kyakhta">Kyakhta</a> borders are the only places where sustained interaction occurs between Mongolia and its neighbors. Other ports are much smaller. The combined population of Altanbulag and Kyakhta is only 25,000 and so does not count as a significant urban agglomeration for cultural exchange. For now Ulaanbaatar remains the main, and almost only, point of contact between Mongolia and its neighbors. Beijing remains the closest <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> to Ulaanbaatar. The UB-Peking corridor is served by busy air, rail and road links.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearances_in_fiction">Appearances in fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ulaanbaatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Appearances in fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Alas,_Babylon" title="Alas, Babylon">Alas, Babylon</a></i> by Pat Frank, the city was a relocation site for the Soviet leadership. In the novel it had a medium-wave station for communications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Library_of_Congress_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_Library_of_Congress-107">[107]</a></sup></p>

<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="padding:0.5em 0 0.3em; line-height:1.3em;">
<div><b>*</b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">Transcontinental country</a>.<br/>
<b>†</b> See: <a href="/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem" title="Positions on Jerusalem">Positions on Jerusalem</a>. Both Israel and Palestinians claim Jerusalem as capital. <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> contains the Israeli parliament and almost all Israeli government ministries. <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> contains most foreign embassies in Israel; <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the administrative seat of the Palestinian Authority.<br/>
<b>+</b> According to the 1947 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Constitution of the Republic of China">Constitution of the Republic of China</a>, Nanjing is the official capital of the ROC, with Taipei as the <a href="/wiki/Temporary_capital" title="Temporary capital">seat of government</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">Political status of Taiwan</a>.</div>
</td>
